OFFICIAL STATEMENT DATED MAY 17, 2022
NEW ISSUE – BOOK-ENTRY-ONLY SYSTEM RATINGS: See “RATINGS” herein.
In the opinion of Gust Rosenfeld P.L.C., Phoenix, Arizona, Bond Counsel, under existing laws, regulations, rulings and 
judicial decisions, and assuming continuing compliance with certain restrictions, conditions and requirements by the Town of 
Gilbert, Arizona Water Resources Municipal Property Corporation and the Town of Gilbert, Arizona, as mentioned under “TAX 
EXEMPTION” herein, interest income on the Bonds is excluded from gross income for federal income tax purposes. Interest 
income on the Bonds is not an item of tax preference to be included in computing the alternative minimum tax. In the opinion of 
Bond Counsel, interest income on the Bonds is exempt from Arizona income taxes. See “TAX EXEMPTION”, “BOND PREMIUM” 
and “ORIGINAL ISSUE DISCOUNT” herein.
$473,005,000
TOWN OF GILBERT, ARIZONA
WATER RESOURCES MUNICIPAL PROPERTY CORPORATION 
SENIOR LIEN UTILITY SYSTEM REVENUE BONDS, SERIES 2022 
(GREEN BONDS)
Dated: Date of Initial Delivery Due: July 15, as shown on inside front cover page.
The Senior Lien Utility System Revenue Bonds, Series 2022 (Green Bonds) (the “Bonds”) are being issued by the Town of Gilbert, 
Arizona, Water Resources Municipal Property Corporation (the “Corporation”) pursuant to a Series 2022 Utilities Bond Indenture, 
to be dated as of June 1, 2022, from the Corporation to U.S. Bank Trust Company, National Association, as trustee (the “Trustee”). 
Interest on the Bonds will be payable semiannually on January 15 and July 15 of each year, commencing January 15, 2023. The 
Bonds will initially be registered in the name of Cede & Co., as nominee of The Depository Trust Company (“DTC”), for purposes of 
the book-entry-only system described herein and will be available to ultimate purchasers in amounts of $5,000 of principal due on 
a specified maturity date or any integral multiple thereof pursuant to the book-entry-only system maintained by DTC. Payments of 
principal and interest with respect to the Bonds will be paid by the Trustee to DTC for subsequent disbursements to DTC participants 
who will remit such payments to the beneficial owners of the Bonds. See APPENDIX I – “Book-Entry-Only System.”
The Bonds will be special, limited revenue obligations of the Corporation and will be payable solely from purchase payments required 
to be paid by the Town of Gilbert, Arizona (the “Town”), to the Corporation pursuant to a Series 2022 Utilities Town Purchase 
Agreement, to be dated as of June 1, 2022 (the “Town Purchase Agreement”), between the Corporation and the Town. The obligation 
of the Town to make the purchase payments and any other obligations of the Town under the Town Purchase Agreement will be 
payable solely from, and secured by a senior lien on and pledge of, revenues received from the operation of the complete waterworks 
and sewer plant and system (the “System”) of the Town, after payment of costs of operation and maintenance, and on a parity of lien 
on such revenues with the Parity Obligations (as defined herein) currently outstanding and any additional obligations issued on a 
parity basis in the future. For a complete description of the definitions of Net Revenues and Operation and Maintenance Expenses, 
see APPENDIX D – “Summary of Certain Provisions of Legal Documents – Certain Definitions.”
Additional Parity Obligations (as defined herein) may, in the future, be issued on a parity basis with the Bonds under certain 
circumstances. See “SECURITY FOR AND SOURCE OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS” herein. The Bonds are being issued by the 
Corporation for the purpose of (i) paying for certain improvements to the System and (ii) paying the costs of issuance of the Bonds. 
See “THE SYSTEM IMPROVEMENTS” herein.
See Maturity Schedule on Inside Front Cover Page
Certain of the Bonds will be subject to redemption prior to maturity as described herein. See “THE BONDS - Redemption Provisions.” 
The Bonds have been identified as “Green Bonds” by Kestrel Verifiers. See APPENDIX H – “Kestrel Verifiers Second Party Opinion.”
THE BONDS WILL BE SPECIAL, LIMITED OBLIGATIONS OF THE CORPORATION, PAYABLE SOLELY FROM THE SOURCES 
HEREIN DESCRIBED. THE BONDS ARE NOT GENERAL OBLIGATIONS OF THE CORPORATION, THE TOWN, THE STATE OF 
ARIZONA OR ANY POLITICAL SUBDIVISION THEREOF, AND THE FULL FAITH AND CREDIT OF THE CORPORATION, THE 
TOWN, THE STATE OF ARIZONA, OR ANY POLITICAL SUBDIVISION THEREOF ARE NOT PLEDGED FOR THE PAYMENT OF 
THE BONDS.
This cover page contains certain information relating to the Bonds for convenience of reference only. It is not a summary of 
material information with respect to the Bonds. Investors must read this Official Statement in its entirety to obtain information 
essential to the making of an informed investment decision with respect to the Bonds.
The Bonds are offered when, as and if issued by the Corporation, and subject to the legal opinion of Gust Rosenfeld P.L.C., Phoenix, 
Arizona, Bond Counsel, as to validity and tax exemption. Certain legal matters will be passed upon for the Underwriters identified 
below by Squire Patton Boggs (US) LLP, Phoenix, Arizona and for the Corporation and the Town by the Town Attorney of the Town. 
It is expected that the Bonds will be available for delivery through the facilities of DTC on or about June 14, 2022.

$473,005,000 
TOWN OF GILBERT, ARIZONA 
WATER RESOURCES MUNICIPAL PROPERTY CORPORATION 
SENIOR LIEN UTILITY SYSTEM REVENUE BONDS, SERIES 2022 
(GREEN BONDS) 
 
INTRODUCTORY STATEMENT 
 
The purpose of this Official Statement, which includes the cove r page, the inside front cover and the Appendices 
attached hereto, is to provide  certain information in connectio n with the offering by the Town of Gilbert, Arizona 
Water Resources Municipal Property Corporation (the “Corporation”) of the $473,005,000 aggregate principal amount 
of Senior Lien Utility System Revenue Bonds, Series 2022 (Green  Bonds) (the “Bonds”) of the Corporation issued 
pursuant to a Series 2022 Utilities Bond Indenture, to be dated  as of June 1, 2022 (the “Indenture”), from the 
Corporation to U.S. Bank Trust Company, National Association, a s trustee (the “Trustee”).  The Bonds are being 
issued by the Corporation to (i) pay for certain improvements ( the “System Improvements”) to the complete 
waterworks and sewer plant and system (the “System”) of the Tow n of Gilbert, Arizona (“Gilbert” or the “Town”) 
and (ii) pay the costs of issuance of the Bonds.  See “THE SYSTEM IMPROVEMENTS.” 
The Bonds will be special, limited obligations of the Corporation, payable solely from payments received pursuant to 
a Series 2022 Utilities Town Purchase Agreement, to be dated as of June 1, 2022 (the “Town Purchase Agreement”), 
between the Town, as purchaser, and the Corporation, as seller, which requires the Town to make payments (“Purchase 
Payments”) to the Trustee in amounts sufficient to pay when due  the principal of and interest on the Bonds, fees of 
the Trustee and all other expenses enumerated in the Town Purch ase Agreement.  Purchase Payments will be made 
solely from Net Revenues (as defined in “APPENDIX D – Summary o f Certain Provisions of Legal Documents” 
herein).  See “SECURITY FOR AND SOURCE OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS.”  The offering of the Bonds is 
made only by way of this Official Statement, which supersedes any other information or materials used in connection 
with the offer or sale of the Bonds.  Accordingly, prospective purchasers of the Bonds should read this entire Official 
Statement before making their investment decisions. 
All financial and other information presented in this Official Statement has been provided by the Town from its 
records, except for information expressly attributed to other s ources.  The presentation of financial and other 
information, including tables of receipts from taxes and other sources, is intended to show recent historical information 
and, except as expressly stated otherwise, is not intended to indicate future or continuing trends in the financial position 
or other affairs of the Town.  No representation is made that p ast experience, as is shown by the financial and other 
information, will necessarily continue or be repeated in the future. 
For definitions of certain capitalized terms used but not other wise defined in this Official Statement and for certain 
provisions of the Town Purchase Agreement and the Indenture, see APPENDIX D – “Summary of Certain Provisions 
of Legal Documents.” 
 
 
THE BONDS 
Authorization and Purpose 
The Bonds are being issued by the Corporation under the terms of the Indenture to pay for certain improvements to 
the System and to pay the costs of issuance of the Bonds.  Purchase Payments will be required to be sufficient to make 
payments of principal and interest on the Bonds.  The Town will make a senior lien pledge of Net Revenues to secure 
amounts due under the Town Purchase Agreement, and on a parity of lien on such revenues with the Parity Obligations 
(as defined herein) currently outstanding and any additional obligations issued in the future.  See “SECURITY FOR 
AND SOURCE OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS.” 
The issuance and delivery of the Bonds, the execution and delivery of the Indenture and the Town Purchase Agreement 
and the application of the proceed s of the Bonds by the Corpora tion were authorized by a resolution adopted by the 
Board of Directors of the Corporation on April 25, 2022.  Appro val of the issuance and delivery of the Bonds, the 
application of the proceeds ther efrom by the Corporation and th e execution and delivery of the Town Purchase 
Agreement were authorized by a resolution adopted by the Mayor and Common Council of the Town (the “Town 
Council”) on April 26, 2022. 2 
 
General Terms 
 
The Bonds will be dated the date of their initial delivery and will bear interest therefrom to the maturity or earlier 
redemption of each of the Bonds payable semiannually on January 15 and July 15 of each year, commencing January 
15, 2023.  The Bonds will bear interest at the rates and will mature on the dates and in the amounts, all as set forth on 
the inside front cover of this Official Statement.  The Bonds i nitially will be registered only in the name of Cede & 
Co., the nominee of The Depository Trust Company (“DTC”) for pu rposes of a book-entry-only system.  Beneficial 
ownership interests in the Bonds may be purchased through direc t and indirect participants of DTC in amounts of 
$5,000 of principal due on a speci fic maturity date or integral  multiples thereof.  See APPENDIX I – “Book-Entry-
Only System.” 
Redemption Provisions 
Optional Redemption.  The Bonds maturing on or after July 15, 2033, will be subject  to redemption, at the option of 
the Corporation, as directed by the Town, in whole or in part at any time in increments of $5,000 of principal amount 
due on a specific maturity date, in any order of maturity as directed by the Town and by lot within a maturity, on July 
15, 2032, and thereafter by payment of the principal amount of each Bond at the redemption price of the principal 
amount to be redeemed, plus the interest accrued to the date fixed for redemption, without premium. 
Mandatory Redemption.  The Bonds maturing July 15, 2047 will be subject to mandatory redemption on the following 
dates and in the following amounts at a price equal to the principal amount thereof plus interest accrued to the date of 
redemption, but without premium: 
 
Redemption Date (July 15) Principal Amount
2043 $7,380,000
2044 7,685,000         
2045 7,995,000         
2046 8,320,000         
*2047* 8,660,000       
*  Maturity Date.
Term Bonds Due July 15, 2047
 
 
Notice of Redemption.  When redemption is authorized or required, the Trustee will give DTC notice of the redemption 
of the Bonds as described herein in APPENDIX I – “Book-Entry-Only System.”  Any redemption will be from such 
maturities as directed by the Town and by lot within a maturity in any manner the Trustee deems fair. Notice of such 
redemption will be given not more than 60 days nor less than 30 days prior to such redemption date. 
 
Notice having been given in the manner provided above, the portions of the Bonds called for redemption will become 
due and payable on the redemption date and if an amount of money sufficient to redeem all the portions of the Bonds 
called for redemption is held by the Trustee on the redemption date, then the portions thereof to be redeemed will not 
be considered outstanding under the Indenture and will cease to bear interest from and after such redemption date. 
 
 
SECURITY FOR AND SOURCE OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS 
 
General 
 
The Bonds will be special, limited obligations of the Corporation, payable solely from Purchase Payments in amounts 
sufficient to pay when due the principal of and interest on the  Bonds, fees of the Trustee and all other expenses 
enumerated in the Town Purchase Agreement.  Purchase Payments will be made solely from Net Revenues.  Purchase 
Payments will be required to be made regardless of damage to th e System or commercial frustration of purpose, 
without right of set-off or counterclaim, regardless of any contingencies and whether or not the Town possesses or 
uses the System.  The obligations of the Town to make Purchase Payments will continue until all Purchase Payments 
and all other amounts due under the Town Purchase Agreement have been paid. 
 3 
 
Pledge 
 
Purchase Payments will be secured by a senior lien on and pledge of Net Revenues, which consist generally of the 
income, monies and receipts derived by the Town from the owners hip, use and operation of the System less all 
Operation and Maintenance Expenses. “Operation and Maintenance Expenses” generally include all expenses 
reasonably incurred in connection with the operation of the System.  Purchase Payments will be on a parity of lien on 
such revenues with the Town of Gilbert, Arizona Water Resources Municipal Property Corporation Senior Lien Utility 
System Revenue and Revenue Refunding Bonds, Series 2016 currently outstanding in the aggregate principal amount 
of $89,390,000 (the “2016 Bonds”), and Town of Gilbert, Arizona Water Resources Municipal Property Corporation 
Senior Lien Utility System Revenue Bonds, Series 2018 currently  outstanding in the aggregate principal amount of 
$27,965,000 (together with the 2016 Bonds, the “Parity Obligati ons”) and any additional obligations issued in the 
future on a parity basis therewith as described under “Addition al Senior Obligations” below. See “SCHEDULE OF  
DEBT SERVICE REQUIREMENTS AND DE BT SERVICE COVERAGE” and APPEND I X  D  –  “ S u m m a r y  o f  
Certain Provisions of Legal Documents – Certain Definitions.”   
 
The obligations of the Town under the Town Purchase Agreement will not constitute a debt or a pledge of the full 
faith and credit of the Town, the State of Arizona (the “State”) or any other political subdivision thereof.  The Town 
will not pledge any form of ad valorem property taxes to the payment of the Bonds.  The Bonds will be special, 
limited obligations of the Corporation, secured only by Purchase Payments which are to be paid from, and secured 
by, a pledge of Net Revenues.  No security interest will be  held by the Trustee for the benefit of the owners of the 
Bonds in any portion of the System.  Remedies available to the Trustee upon a failure of the Town to make Purchase 
Payments when due will be generally limited to specific performance against the Town to payment from Net 
Revenues.  For a description of events of default an d remedies under the Town Purchase Agreement, see 
APPENDIX D – “Summary of Certain Provisions of Legal Documents - The Town Purchase Agreement – Events 
of Default” and “Remedies on Default by Town.”  The Town may, but will not be required to, pay amounts due 
under the Town Purchase Agreement from any other money legally available for such purposes. 
For a discussion about the System, see APPENDIX A – “The System .”  For a discussion of certain covenants which 
the Town has entered into with respect to the System, see APPENDIX D – “Summary of Certain Provisions of Legal 
Documents – The Town Purchase Agreement.” 
Additional Senior Obligations 
In order to issue additional parity lien obligations pursuant t o the requirements of the Town Purchase Agreement 
(“Additional Parity Obligations” and, together with the Parity Obligations and the Bonds, “Senior Obligations”), 
which obligations would be on a parity basis with payments to b e made under the Town Purchase Agreement, the 
Town will be required to file a statement by the Finance and Ma nagement Services Director of the Town or an 
independent certified public accountant to the effect that the aggregate amount of Net Revenues for the last full Fiscal 
Year immediately preceding the i ssuance of any Additional Parity Obligations were equal to the sum of (i) not less 
than one hundred twenty-five percent (125%) of Parity Lien Test  Debt Service (as defined in Appendix D hereto), 
including the obligations proposed to be issued, (ii) not less than one hundred percent (100%) of the aggregate amounts 
payable in such Fiscal Year and secured on a subordinate basis by Net Revenues and (iii) not less than one hundred 
percent (100%) of any additional amounts required to maintain o r fund necessary fund balances under the Town 
Purchase Agreement or Parity Obligation Documents.  The Town Purchase Agreement will permit certain adjustments 
to Net Revenues in such report or statement by the Finance and Management Services Director or independent certified 
public accountant.  The Town Purchase Agreement will also permit the issuance of Additional Parity Obligations for 
refunding purposes without compliance with the foregoing financ ial tests if certain other conditions are met.  See 
APPENDIX D – “Summary of Certain Provisions of Legal Documents – The Town Purchase Agreement – Parity 
Obligations for Refunding Purposes” and – “Additional Parity Obligations Generally.” 
Subordinate Lien Obligations 
The Town Purchase Agreement does not prohibit the issuance or incurrence by the Town of obligations payable from 
Net Revenues on a basis subordinate to the Senior Obligations.  The Town currently does not have any subordinate 
lien obligations and has no present plans to issue or incur any such subordinate lien obligations. 4 
 
Rate Covenant; Other Covenants 
 
Pursuant to the Town Purchase Agreement, the Town will covenant to continuously own, control, operate and maintain 
the System in an efficient and economical manner and on a reven ue-producing basis and will at all times, establish, 
fix, maintain and collect rates, fees and other charges for all utility services furnished by the System fully sufficient: 
 
1) To pay the Operation and Maintenance Expenses; 
 
2) To produce an aggregate amount of Net Revenues in each Fiscal Y ear equal to the sum of (i) one 
hundred twenty-five percent (125%) of Interest Requirement and Principal Requirement for the then

THE TOWN OF GILBERT 
 
The Town is a municipal corporation organized and existing unde r the laws of the State.  For economic and 
demographic information on the Town, see APPENDIX B – “Town of Gilbert, Arizona – General Economic and 
Demographic Information.” 
 
 
THE CORPORATION 
 
The Corporation is a nonprofit corporation incorporated on February 5, 1997 and existing pursuant to the laws of the 
State.  The Corporation is permitted, pursuant to its Articles of Incorporation, to conduct all lawful affairs for which 
nonprofit corporations may be in corporated pursuant to the laws  of the State, subject to the express limitation and 
condition that the Corporation will always be operated solely and exclusively in the interest of the general public.  The 
Corporation exists and acts as a separate entity.  The Board of Directors of the Corporation presently consists of five 
members appointed by the Town Council. 
 
The Corporation has the power to incur indebtedness and to issu e bonds, to own real property, to provide for the 
acquisition and construction of a utility system facility, to lease such facility to the Town and to exercise any and all 
rights and powers which a nonprofit corporation organized under the laws of the State may now or hereafter exercise.  
Upon the dissolution of the Corporation, all of its assets rema ining after payment of or provision for payment of all 
debts and liabilities will be distributed to the Town. 
 
The Corporation has no stockholders or members.  Vacancies occurring on the Board of Directors of the Corporation 
are filled by appointment of the Town Council.  Members of the Board of Directors may be removed, with or without 
cause, by the Town Council.  All amendments to the Articles of Incorporation or Bylaws of the Corporation require 
approval by the Town Council.  No compensation is paid to any officer or director of the Corporation. 
 
 
THE SYSTEM IMPROVEMENTS 
 
The System Improvements described below will be purchased by the Town from the Corporation pursuant to the Town 
Purchase Agreement.  A portion of the proceeds from the sale of the Bonds will be used to pay the costs of the System 
Improvements.  Such portion of the proceeds of the sale of the Bonds will be deposited with and held by the Town 
and used to pay the costs of the System Improvements.  Moneys deposited with the Town and used to purchase 
the System Improvements will not be pledged as security for the  Bonds.  For a more complete rendition of the 
terms relating to the use of proceeds of the Bonds see APPENDIX  D – “Summary of Certain Provisions of Legal 
Documents – The Town Purchase Agreement.” 
 
System Improvements include the non-growth related reconstruction of the North Water Treatment Plant (“NWTP”) 
and other non-growth water projects that are included in the ca pital improvement plan (“CIP”) of the Town.  The 
NWTP is a surface water treatment  plant located on a Town-owned parcel south of Guadalupe Road between 
Greenfield and Higley Roads.  The non-growth related portion of the NWTP project will rebuild the existing 45 million 
gallons per day (“MGD”) facility and will be repaid with a combination of funding sources including water operating 
revenue (for the added infrastructure related to water quality) , and water repair and replacement funds (for the 
replacement of the existing 45 MGD  infrastructure). Any current  structures that have sufficient useful life will be 
reused and incorporated into the new facility. Other non-growth  related water projects anticipated to be completed 
include repair and replacement of  certain water lines throughout the Town and may include the purchase of water 
rights. 
 
System Improvements also include the growth related portions of the NWTP and other related water projects that are 
included in the most recently adopted CIP.  The growth related portion of the NWTP project will expand the existing 
45 MGD facility into a 60 MGD facility and will be repaid with water system development fees.  Other growth related 
water projects anticipated to be completed include those identified in the system development fee study, and may 
include the purchase of water rights.  Design of the NWTP project is already underway and construction is anticipated 
to be completed by the end of calendar year 2026. 
 
Gilbert expects to post updates on the System Improvements on the Town’s website: www.gilbertaz.gov.  The Town 
intends to produce a report aft er all Bond proceeds have been e xpended that will include a summary of financed 
projects and their impacts. Impact metrics are expected to incl ude: number of customers benefiting from the System 7 
 
Improvements, total increase in treatment capacity, and reduced  reliance on groundwater resources as a result of the 
financed activities. The Town will voluntarily post this report  on either the Town’s website or on the Electronic 
Municipal Market Access system  (“EMMA”) of the Municipal Secur ities Rulemaking Board (“MSRB”) after all 
Bond proceeds have been spent. 
 
 
DESIGNATION OF BONDS AS GREEN BONDS 
 
Green Bonds Designation 
 
Per the International Capital Market Association (“ICMA”), Green Bonds are any type of bond instrument where the 
proceeds will be exclusively applied to finance or re-finance, in part or in full, new and/or existing eligible Green 
Projects and which are aligned with the four core components of the Green Bond Principles. The four core components 
are: 1. Use of Proceeds; 2. Process for Project Evaluation and Selection; 3. Management of Proceeds; and 4. Reporting. 
 
Kestrel Verifiers has determined that the Bonds are in conformance with the four core components of the ICMA Green 
Bond Principles, as described in Kestrel Verifiers’ “Second Party Opinion”, which is attached hereto as APPENDIX 
H. 
 
Despite the Second Party Opinion being provided by Kestrel Verifiers, it should be noted that there is currently no 
clearly defined regulatory definition applicable to the Bonds as to what constitutes a “green” or equivalently labeled 
project or as to what precise attributes are required for a particular project to be defined as “green” or such other 
equivalent label.  No assurance can be given that a regulatory definition will develop over time, or that, if developed, 
it will include the projects to be financed or refinanced with the proceeds of the Bonds.  
 
Independent Second Party Opinion on Green Bonds Designation and Disclaimer 
 
For over 20 years, Kestrel Verifiers has been consulting in sustainable finance. Kestrel Verifiers, a division of Kestrel 
360, Inc. is an Approved Verifier accredited by the Climate Bon ds Initiative and an Observer for the ICMA Green 
Bond Principles and Social Bond Principles. Kestrel Verifiers reviews transactions in all asset classes worldwide for 
alignment with ICMA Green Bond Principles, Social Bond Principles, Sustainability Bond Guidelines and the Climate 
Bonds Initiative Standards and Criteria.  
 
The Second Party Opinion issued by Kestrel Verifiers does not and is not intended to make any representation or give 
any assurance with respect to any other matter relating to the Bonds. Designations by Kestrel Verifiers are not a 
recommendation to any person to purchase, hold, or sell the Bonds and such labeling does not address the market price 
or suitability of these Bonds for a particular investor and doe s not and is not in any way intended to address the 
likelihood of timely payment of interest or principal when due. 
 
In issuing the Second Party Opinion, Kestrel Verifiers has assumed and relied upon the accuracy and completeness of 
the information made publicly available by the Town or that was otherwise made available to Kestrel Verifiers.

RISK FACTORS 
Investment in the Bonds involves risks that may not be appropriate for certain investors.  The following is a 
discussion of certain risk factors that should be considered, in addition to other matters set forth herein, in 
evaluating the Bonds for investment.  The information set forth below does not purport to be an exhaustive listing 
of the risks and other considerations that may be relevant to an investment in the Bonds.  In addition, the order in 
which the following information is presented is not intended to reflect the relative importance of any such risks. 
Limited Obligations 
The obligation of the Town under the Town Purchase Agreement will not constitute a debt or a pledge of the full faith 
and credit of the Town, the State or any other political subdivision thereof. The Town will not pledge any form of ad 
valorem property taxes to the payment of the Bonds. The Bonds will be special, limited obligations of the Corporation 
secured only by Purchase Payments which are to be paid from and  secured by a pledge of Net Revenues. The 
Corporation has no other source of revenues from which to pay debt service on the Bonds.  The Corporation has no 
taxing power.  No security interest will be held by the Trustee for the benefit of the owners of the Bonds in any portion 
of the System. Remedies available to the Trustee upon a failure  of the Town to make Purchase Payments when due 
will be generally limited to specific performance against the Town to payment from Net Revenues. 
No assurance can be made that Net Revenues, estimated or otherw ise, will be realized by the Town in amounts 
sufficient to pay Purchase Payments.  In addition, the realizat ion of future Net Revenues is subject to, among other 
things, the capabilities of management of the Town, the ability  of the Town to provide water or wastewater services 
to its customers, and the ability of the Town to meet its coven ant to fix, prescribe, and co llect rates and charges for 
the System in amounts sufficient to timely pay Purchase Payment s ,  w h i c h  c o u l d  i n  t u r n  a d v e r s e l y  i m p a c t  t h e  
Corporation’s ability to make payments of the principal of or i nterest on the Bonds.  See “SECURITY FOR AND 
SOURCE OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS – Rate Covenant; Other Covenants.” Additional Senior Obligations may 
be incurred in the future that are secured, on a parity with the Bonds, by Net Revenues.  See “SECURITY FOR AND 
SOURCE OF PAYMENT OF THE BONDS – Additional Parity Obligations.” 
No Debt Service Reserve Fund 
Neither the Town nor the Corporation have covenanted to, and wi ll be under no obligation to, create and maintain a 
debt service reserve fund for the payment of principal of or interest on the Bonds.  
System Expenses and Future Rates 
Increases in expenses could require a significant increase in rates or charges in order to pay for projects and to pay the 
debt service on any Senior Obligations, including, without limitation, Purchase Payments securing the Bonds.  Also, 
any such rate increases could increase the likelihood of nonpay ment by purchasers of water or wastewater services 
from the Town and could also decrease demand from such purchase rs and may impact the Town’s ability to make 
Purchase Payments, which could in turn adversely impact the Corporation’s ability to make payments of the principal 
of and interest on the Bonds. 
System Demand 
There can be no assurance that the local demand for the services provided by the System will be maintained at levels 
described in this Official Statement.  Because of the potential  for changes in demographics within the boundaries of 
the Town, it is possible for the demand for water or wastewater services to decline over t he term of the Bonds.  A 
significant decline in demand might create a situation in which the Town could not increase rates sufficiently to offset 
the decrease in customers or usage.  This would reduce the Town ’s ability to make Purchase Payments, which could 
in turn adversely impact the Corporation’s ability to make paym ents of the principal of and interest on the Bonds as 
and when due. 
Water Supply and Drought Conditions 
The ability of the System to operate effectively can be affecte d by the water supply available to the Town, which is 
situated in a desert environment.   If the water supply decrease s significantly, whether by operation or mandatory 
supply restrictions, prohibitively high water costs or otherwise, System sales may diminish and Net Revenues 11 
 
available to pay Purchase Payments may be adversely affected.  The Town has planned and managed reserve supplies 
to account for normal occurrences of drought conditions.   
The Colorado River system has experienced over-allocation and extensive drought conditions for 18 years, resulting 
in Lake Mead dropping to historically low reservoir levels.  As  reservoir levels in Lake Mead drop, different tiers of 
water supply reductions affect the State, California, Nevada and Mexico.  The water level elevation is approximately 
1,062 feet as of March 27, 2022.  A tier 1 reduction occurs whe n the water level falls below 1,075 feet; a tier 2a 
reduction occurs when water levels fall below 1,050 feet, a tier 2b reduction occurs when water levels fall below 1,045 
feet and a tier 3 reduction occurs when water levels fall below 1,025 feet.  The Town’s water supply that comes from 
the Colorado River System will be reduced by varying percentages for each of the shortage tiers starting in 2023, with 
the largest reductions occurring with tier 3.  A tier 3 reducti on results in a temporary reduction of approximately 8% 
of the Town’s total water portfolio.  See APPENDIX A – “The Water System.” 
Security of the System 
To ensure water quality and delivery service are maintained, the Town continually plans and prepares for emergency 
situations such as fire, power failure, or possible terrorist activities.  The Town routinely monitors the water supply 
for possible contamination in a variety of ways, including taki ng thousands of water samples throughout the year.  
Additional emergency preparation procedures include: routinely training staff on critical security and safety; 
conducting disaster drills to improve coordination efforts throughout the region; collaborating with law enforcement 
and fire-rescue agencies in order to improve multiple agency re sponse to water emergencies; implementing a water 
quality notification plan to keep customers informed in emergen cy situations; and implementing additional security 
measures throughout the System.   
There can be no assurance that any existing or additional safety and security measures will prove adequate in the event 
of an emergency situation affecting the System, or that costs o f security measures will not be greater than presently 
anticipated.  Further, damage to certain components of the Syst em could require the Town to increase expenditures 
for repairs to the System significantly enough to adversely imp act the Town’s ability to make Purchase Payments, 
which could in turn adversely impact the Corporation’s ability to make payments of the principal of and interest on 
the Bonds.   
Cybersecurity 
The Town, like many other public and private entities, relies o n computer and other digital networks and systems to 
conduct its operations, including the operation of the System.  As a recipient and provider of personal, private or other 
sensitive electronic information, the Town is potentially subject to multiple cyber threats, including without limitation 
hacking, viruses, ransomware, malware and other attacks. United States government agencies have in the past issued 
warnings indicating that critical infrastructure sectors such as water systems may be specific targets of cybersecurity 
threats. 
 
The Town has established a comprehensive Written Information Se curity Program (“WISP”) to manage operational 
concerns associated with Information Technology, data processing, and cybersecurity.  This WISP includes defining, 
documenting, and supporting the implementation and maintenance of the administrative, technical, and physical 
safeguards focused on maintaining the confidentiality, integrit y, and availability of the Town’s data.  These include 
appropriate governance bodies and mechanisms to provide operati onal oversight and enforcement, continual risk 
assessment and mitigation, development of information security policies and procedures, implementation of task 
specific safeguards, partnering with industry leaders in service provision of cloud, monitoring, and security services, 
and establishing incident response strategies to address potential events and incidents.  
 
No assurance can be given that the Town’s efforts to manage cyber threats and attacks will be successful in all cases, 
or that any such attack will not materially impact the operatio ns or finances of the Town or disrupt the operation of 
the System.  As of the date of this Official Statement, there have been no detected cyberattacks that have affected the 
System. 
 
Factors Adversely Affecting Development 
System development fees are paid to the Town as building permits are issued for the construction of new homes and 
other structures. The pace at w hich building permits are issued  will be affected by changes in general economic 12 
 
conditions, material shortages, fluctuations in land prices bot h locally and nationally, availability of water, water 
treatment, sewage treatment and power necessary for development , changes in the income tax treatment of land and 
ownership, changes in the availability and cost of borrowed funds including mortgages for homebuyers, inflation and 
numerous other factors. In addition, land development operations are subject to comprehensive federal, State and local 
regulation. Approval is required from various agencies in connection with the layout and design of developments, the 
nature and extent of improvements, the availability of an assured water supply, construction activity, land use, zoning, 
school and health requirements and many other matters. 
In areas of substantial growth, such as the Town, public and or political attitudes toward growth are subject to shifts 
from support for growth to opposition to growth. Although growt h cannot be prevented, no assurance can be given 
that the Town Council as now constituted or a future Town Counc il will not delay or defer action required for 
continued growth. Such action by the Town Council as now consti t u t e d  o r  a  f u t u r e  T o w n  C o u n c i l  c o u l d  h a v e  a  
materially adverse impact on future Net Revenues.  See APPENDIX A – “The System – System Development Fees.” 
Limitations on Remedies 
Any remedies available to the owners of the Bonds upon the occurrence of an Event of Default will be in many respects 
dependent upon judicial actions, which are often subject to discretion and delay and could prove both expensive and 
time consuming to obtain. 
Further, enforceability of the rights and remedies of the owners of the Bonds, and the obligations incurred by the 
Town, may become subject to the federal bankruptcy code and app licable bankruptcy, insolvency, receivership, 
reorganization, moratorium, or similar laws relating to or affecting the enforcement of creditor’s rights generally, now 
or hereafter in effect, equity p rinciples that may limit the sp ecific enforcement under State law of certain remedies, 
the exercise by the United States  of America of the powers dele gated to it by the Constitution, the reasonable and 
necessary exercise, in certain exceptional situations, of the police powers inherent in the sovereignty of the State and 
its governmental bodies in the interest of serving a significan t and legitimate public purpose, and the limitations on 
remedies against counties in the State.  Bankruptcy proceedings , or the exercise of powers by the federal or State 
government, if initiated, could subject the owners of the Bonds to judicial discretion and interpretation of their rights 
in bankruptcy or otherwise and consequently may entail risks of delay, limitation, or modification of their rights.  The 
opinion to be delivered by Bond Counsel (as defined herein), co ncurrently with the issuance of the Bonds, that the 
Bonds constitute valid and binding limited obligations of the C orporation and the Indenture constitutes a valid and 
binding obligation of the Corporation will be subject to such l imitations and the various other legal opinion to be 
delivere d conc ur rently with the iss ua nce  of  the  Bonds  wil l be  similarly qualified.  See “APPENDIX F – Form of 
Approving Opinion.” 
If the Town fails to comply with its covenants under the Town P urchase Agreement to pay the Purchase Payments, 
there can be no assurance of the availability of remedies adequate to protect the interests of the holders of the Bonds. 
Statutory and Regulatory Compliance; Future Legislation 
The System is subject to a variety of federal and State statuto ry and regulatory requirements.  Laws and regulations 
governing water and wastewater treatment and the delivery of water are enacted and promulgated by federal, state and 
local government agencies.  Compliance with these laws and regulations is and will continue to be costly and, as more 
stringent standards are developed to ensure safe drinking water standards and the provision of water for other purposes, 
such costs will likely increase. 
The Town’s failure to comply with applicable laws and regulations could result in significant fines and penalties.  
Such claims are payable from assets of the System or from other legally available sources.  In addition to claims by 
private parties, changes in the scope and standards for public agency water and wastewater systems such as that 
operated by the Town may also lead to administrative orders issued by federal or State regulators.  The Town is unable 
to predict the adoption or amendment of any such laws, rules or  regulations, or their effect on the operations of the 
System or financial condition of the Town.  Future compliance with such orders can also impose substantial additional 
costs on the System.   
No assurance can be given that the cost of compliance with such laws, regulations, and orders would not adversely 
affect the ability of the System to generate Net Revenues sufficient to pay the debt service on any Senior Obligation, 13 
 
including, without limitation, the Purchase Payments, which could in turn adversely impact the Corporation’s ability 
to make payments of the principal of and interest on the Bonds.   
Limited Secondary Market for the Bonds 
There can be no guarantee that there will ever be a secondary market for purchase or sale of the Bonds or, if a secondary 
market exists, that the Bonds can be sold for any particular price.  Occasionally, because of general market conditions 
or because of adverse history or economic prospects connected with a particular issue, secondary marketing practices 
in connection with a particular i ssue are suspended or terminated.  Additionally, prices of issues for which a market 
is being made will depend upon then prevailing circumstances. S uch prices could be substantially different from the 
original purchase price. 
Loss of Tax Exemption on the Bonds 
As discussed under the caption “TAX EXEMPTION,” interest on the Bonds could become included in gross income 
for purposes of federal income taxation, retroactive to the dat e the Bonds were issued, as a result of future acts or 
omissions of the Town or the Corporation in violation of their respective covenants in the Indenture and the Town 
Purchase Agreement.  In that event, the Bonds are not subject to special redemption and will remain outstanding on a 
taxable basis until maturity or redeemed in accordance with the redemption provisions contained in the Indenture. 
Economic, Political, Social, and Environmental Conditions 
Prospective investors are encouraged to evaluate current and pr ospective economic, political, social, and 
environmental conditions as part of an informed investment deci sion.  Changes in economic, political, social, or 
environmental conditions on a local, state, federal, and/or int ernational level may adversely affect investment risk 
generally.  Such conditional changes may include (but are not limited to) fluctuations in business production, consumer 
prices, or financial markets, un employment rates, technological  advancements, shortages or surpluses in natural 
resources or energy supplies, changes in law, social unrest, fluctuations in the crime rate, political conflict, acts of war 
or terrorism, environmental damage, and natural disasters. The Town cannot guarantee that prices for electricity will 
not increase, which could adversely affect the System’s financial condition.   
Covid-19  
The Coronavirus Disease 2019 (“COVID-19”) global pandemic continues to affect the nation and the State with ongoing 
concerns related to health and safety, appropriate preventative protocols, fiscal and economic issues, and student learning loss. 
At present, government and business operations in the State, following the rescindment of numerous COVID-19-related 
Executive Orders by Arizona Governor Doug Ducey, essentially function without government-imposed restrictions relating 
to the pandemic. 
The Town does not currently anticipate the collection of Revenu es and the ability of the Town to pay Purchase 
Payments to be materially adversely affected by the continued existence of COVID-19.  Neither the Corporation nor 
the Town, however, can predict the effect the on-going spread of COVID-19 (including COVID-19 variants such as the 
Delta and Omicron variants or future, similar variants) or the various governmental or private actions taken in response to 
COVID-19 will have on the finances or operations of the Town or the System, which could have a negative impact on the 
Net Revenues pledged to pay operating expenses and debt service of the Bonds, if for example, the customers of the System 
become unable to pay the amounts billed for use of the System. The full financial effect of COVID-19 on the Town and the 
System could change significantly as circumstances and events evolve. The Town will monitor events as they occur, 
particularly those that may have a material adverse effect on the Net Revenues.

TAX EXEMPTION 
 
In the opinion of Bond Counsel, under existing laws, regulation s, rulings and judicial decisions, and assuming 
continuing compliance with certain restrictions, conditions and  requirements by the Corporation and the Town as 
described below, interest income on the Bonds is excluded from gross income for federal income tax purposes. In the 
opinion of Bond Counsel, interest income on the Bonds is exempt  from State income taxes. The opinion of Bond 
Counsel will be dated as of the date of initial delivery of the Bonds. The form of such opinion is included as APPENDIX 
F – “Form of Approving Opinion” attached hereto. 
 
The Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended, (the “Code”) imp oses various restrictions, conditions and 
requirements relating to the continued exclusion of interest income on the Bonds from gross income for federal income 
tax purposes, including a requirement that the Corporation and the Town rebate to the federal government certain of its 
investment earnings with respect to the Bonds. The Corporation and the Town has covenanted to comply with the 
provisions of the Code relating to such matters. Failure to comply with such restrictions, conditions and requirements 
could result in the interest income on the Bonds being included as gross income for federal income tax purposes, under 
certain circumstances, from the date of initial issuance. The Bonds do not provide for an adjustment in the interest rate 
or yield in the event of taxability and an event of taxability does not cause an acceleration of the principal on the Bonds. 
The opinion of Bond Counsel assumes continuing compliance with such covenants. 
 
The Code also imposes an “alternative minimum tax” upon certain  individuals. A taxpayer’s “alternative minimum 
taxable income” (“AMTI”) is its taxable income with certain adjustments. Interest income on the Bonds is not an item 
of tax preference to be included in the AMTI. 
 
Although Bond Counsel will render an opinion that, as of the de livery date of the Bonds, interest income on the 
Bonds is excluded from gross income for federal income tax purposes, the accrual or receipt of interest on the Bonds
 
may otherwise affect a Beneficial Owner’s (as defined in APPEND IX I – “Book-Entry-Only System”)  federal tax 
liability. Certain taxpayers may experience other tax consequen ces. Taxpayers who become Beneficial  Owners of 
the Bonds, including without limitation, corporations subject t o the branch profits tax, financial institutions, certain 
insurance companies, certain subchapter S corporations, individ uals who receive Social Security or Railroad 
Retirement benefits and taxpayers who have or are deemed to hav e incurred indebtedness to purchase or carry tax-
exempt obligations, should consult their tax advisors as to the applicability of such tax consequences to the respective 
Beneficial Owner. The nature and extent of these other tax cons equences will depend upon the Beneficial Owner’s 
particular tax status and the Be neficial Owner’s other items of  income or deduction. Bond Counsel expresses no 
opinion regarding any such other tax consequences. 
 
The Bonds are not “private activity bonds” within the meaning of Section 141 of the Code. 
 
Currently and from time to time, there are legislative proposals in Congress, which, if enacted or made effective, could 
alter or amend the federal tax matters referred to above or adversely affect the market value and marketability (liquidity) 
of the Bonds. Any such change that occurs before initial delive ry of the Bonds could cause Bond Counsel to deliver 
opinion substantially different from the opinion shown in APPENDIX F – “Form of Approving Opinion.” The extent 15 
 
of change in Bond Counsel’s opinion cannot be determined at this time. It cannot be predicted whether, when or in what 
form any such proposal or proposals might be enacted or whether, if enacted, such proposal or proposals would apply 
to obligations (such as the Bonds) issued prior to the enactment or effective date. Prospective purchasers should consult 
with their own tax advisors regarding any other pending or proposed federal income tax legislation. 
 
 
BOND PREMIUM 
 
The initial public offering prices of the Bonds maturing on Jul y 15, 2023, through and including July 15, 2038 
(collectively, the “Premium Bond s”), are greater than the amoun t payable on each Bond at maturity.   An amount 
equal to the difference between the initial public offering price of a Premium Bond (assuming that a substantial amount 
o f  t h e  P r e m i u m  B o n d s  o f  t h a t  m a t u r i t y  a r e  s o l d  t o  t h e  p u b l i c  a t such price) and the amount payable at maturity 
constitutes premium to the initial Beneficial Owner of such Premium Bonds. The basis for federal income tax purposes 
of a Premium Bond in the hands of such initial Beneficial Owner must be reduced each year by the amortizable bond 
premium, although no federal income tax deduction is allowed as  a result of such reduction in basis for amortizable 
bond premium. Such reduction in basis will increase the amount of any gain (or decrease the amount of any loss) to 
be recognized for federal income tax purposes upon a sale or ot her taxable disposition of a Premium Bond.  The 
amount of premium that is amortizable each year by an initial Beneficial Owner is determined by using such Beneficial 
Owner's yield to maturity. Beneficial Owners of the Premium Bonds should consult with their own tax advisors with 
respect to the determination of amortizable bond premium with respect to the Premium Bonds for Federal income tax 
purposes and with respect to the state and local tax consequences of owning Premium Bonds. 
 
 
ORIGINAL ISSUE DISCOUNT 
 
The initial offering prices of the Bonds maturing on July 15, 2039, through and including July 15, 2042 and July 15, 
2047 (collectively, the “Discount Bonds”), are less than the re spective amounts payable at maturity. As a result, the 
Discount Bonds will be considered to be issued with original issue discount. The difference between the initial public 
offering price (assuming it is the first price at which a substantial amount of that maturity of Discount Bonds was sold 
(the “OID Issue Price”)) of the Discount Bonds, and the amount payable at maturity of the Discount Bonds will be 
treated as “original issue discount.”  With respect to a Beneficial Owner who purchases a Discount Bond in the initial 
public offering at the OID Issue Price and who holds the Discount Bond to maturity, the full amount of original issue 
discount will constitute interest income which is not includibl e in the gross income of the Beneficial Owner of the 
Discount Bond for federal income tax purposes and Arizona income tax purposes and that Beneficial Owner will not, 
under present federal income tax law and present Arizona income tax law, realize a taxable capital gain upon payment 
of the Discount Bond at maturity.  
 
The original issue discount on each of the Discount Bonds is tr eated for federal income tax purposes and Arizona 
income tax purposes as accreting daily over the term of such Di scount Bond on the basis of a constant interest rate 
compounded at the end of each six-month period (or shorter period from the date of original issue) ending on January 
15 and July 15 (with straight-line interpolation between compounding dates).  
 
The amount of original issue discount accruing each period will be added to the Beneficial Owner’s tax basis for the 
Discount Bond. The adjusted tax basis will be used to determine taxable gain or loss upon disposition of the Discount 
Bond. An initial Beneficial Owner of a Discount Bond who dispos es of the Discount Bond prior to maturity should 
consult his or her tax advisor as to the amount of the original  issue discount accrued over the period held and the 
amount of taxable gain or loss upon the sale or disposition of the Discount Bond prior to maturity.  
 
The Code contains certain provi sions relating to the accretion of original issue discount in the case of subsequent 
Beneficial Owners of the Discount Bonds. Beneficial Owners who do not purchase the Discount Bonds in the initial 
of
fering at the OID Issue Price should consult their own tax ad visors with respect to the tax consequences of the 
ownership of Discount Bonds.  
 
A portion of the original issue discount that accretes in each year to a Beneficial Owner of a Discount Bond may result 
in certain collateral federal income tax consequences as described in “TAX EXEMPTION” herein. Beneficial Owners 
of Discount Bonds in states other than Arizona should consult their own tax advisors with respect to the state and local 
tax consequences of owning Discount Bonds.

 APPENDIX A 
 
THE SYSTEM 
 
General 
The Town provides water treatment, storage and delivery service s and wastewater collection and treatment services 
to its citizens.  It operates water treatment plants and distri bution networks (the “Water System”) and wastewater 
treatment reclamation plants and recharge facilities (the “Wast ewater System” and, with the Water System, the 
“System”).  Charges for services and system development fees pay the direct expenses and overhead costs associated 
with the System’s operations, as well as the debt service on the Bonds.  
System Finances 
The tables on the following pages contain certain information concerning the rates, fees and charges for the System. 
The last rate increase for the Wastewater System was effective November 1, 2018.  The Town implemented an 
increase in Water System rates effective April 1, 2022.   
 
In addition to revenues from rates, fees and charges to the System, the Town also charges utility system development 
fees (the “System Development Fees” or “SDFs”) for residential and commercial connection to the System.  The 
SDFs are one-time charges paid by developers.  The Town’s SDFs are periodically reviewed and updated. Certain 
changes to the Town’s water, water resources and wastewater SDFs were adopted in August 2017 and took effect in 
October of 2017.  Gilbert has completed an updated comprehensiv e SDF review with updated fees, which was 
approved by Town Council March 2022 with a June 2022 implementation date. SDF reviews are conducted every 2 
years. 
 
 
THE WATER SYSTEM 
The Town’s planning area for its water resources consists of ap proximately 76 square miles of which approximately 
55 square miles are within the Town’s existing corporate limits and approximately 21 square miles are within the area 
that has been “strip annexed” or planned for future Town annexation.  There are two smaller private water companies 
operating wells on the southern perimeter of the strip annexed area with fewer than 25 customers each. 
The Town has an Integrated Water Resources Master Plan (the “Plan”) which is updated every five years to ensure an 
adequate water supply.  The Plan addresses water supply managem ent during periods of normal and reduced water 
supply and provides an action plan for ensuring the delivery of  water to its customers.  The Town can enhance its 
water supply as necessary through guidelines that include: shif ting deliveries of surface water from storage facilities 
for recharge credits to treatment plants for direct use; continuing the well maintenance program as backup supply for 
the recovery of stored water; applying to the State for a droug ht pumping exemption if necessary; increasing well 
pumping to access groundwater res erves and stored water reserve s; if Salt River Project (the “SRP”) supplies are 
reduced, purchasing excess Central Arizona Project (the “CAP”) water, if available; closely monitoring watershed 
conditions; and, if available, increasing supplies by utilizing emergency connections with other municipal partners. 
The Town’s 19 wells located thr oughout the service area have th e capacity to produce nearly 42 MGD of potable 
water.  A total of 28 potable wells are planned to help meet wa ter demand at Town build-out with an expected 
production capacity of 58 MGD.  The distribution system include s over 1,200 miles of underground piping, ranging 
from 48 inches in the backbone system, to 4 inch residential distribution mains.   
The Town has two water treatment plants: the NWTP and the San T an Vista Water Treatment Plant (the “SVWTP”, 
and, with the NWTP, the “Water Treatment Plants”).  The NWTP gets its water from SRP and is treated conventionally 
by way of coagulation, flocculation, sedimentation and filtrati on.  It can produce as much as 45 MGD and has a 16 
million gallon reservoir.  The SVWTP receives water from the CAP operated in partnership with the City of Chandler, 
Arizona (“Chandler”) and is treat ed using ballasted flocculatio n. It can produce as much as 48 MGD, 24 MGD of 
which is reserved for use by the Town, and has 12 million gallons of storage capacity.  The Town also utilizes 
disinfected groundwater for high demand periods and during canal maintenance. 
The Town employs approximately 97 persons within three division s (production, distribution and metering).  At the 
start of calendar year 2022, the Water System serviced 89,016 a ccounts, 83,418 of which were residential, 4,143 of 
which were commercial/industrial, 248 of which were schools and 353 of which were municipal.   A-2 
The Town plans to add capacity to the Water System to support g rowth and the demand requirements at build-out, 
with the construction of additional wells and with the addition of surface treatment capacity through plant expansion.  
Future demand is based on existing demand plus current water us e data for specific land use types projected for the 
general plan build-out. 
Water Supplies 
 
The Town has a diverse water resources portfolio made up of surface water supplies from watersheds within Arizona 
(the Salt and Verde Rivers), and from the Colorado River. The T own also currently operates a total of 19 potable 
groundwater production wells, 13 of which are owned by the Town and six of which are owned by Salt River Project. 
Gilbert also utilizes 100% of its reclaimed water supply, reduc ing the demand for potable water used for landscape 
watering throughout the Town's planning area. 
 
The following water resources are the major components of the T own's existing water resources portfolio, each of 
which is discussed in detail: 
 
1. Salt River Project 
2. Roosevelt Water Conservation District (“RWCD”) 
3. Colorado River Supplies 
4. Groundwater 
5. Reclaimed Water 
 
Salt River Project:  SRP is a public power and water utility that provides electric and water service to certain lands 
located within Gilbert. These specific lands were used as collateral during the early 1900’s against the loan from the 
federal government to build the Roosevelt Dam, which impounds w ater from the 13,000 squ are mile watershed in 
northern and eastern Arizona. SR P now operates six reservoirs o n the Salt and Verde River watershed, supplying 
water to over 240,000 acres in the metro Phoenix area. The SRP water supplies are delivered to Gilbert through the 
Eastern Canal, and are available for use only On-Project, or la nds that were originally committed to the Salt River 
Valley Water Users Association. Rights to the SRP water are app urtenant to the lands with in the SRP District, and 
with few exceptions, the right stays with the land, thus “On-Pr oject.” These lands generally include the areas within 
the Town's planning boundary that are west of the Eastern Canal, which total nearly 16,000 acres. As the On-Project 
lands develop, the water is “cut over” to Gilbert for treatment and delivery to the landowner through the municipal 
water distribution system. Approximately 12,000 acres of SRP On-Project lands have been cut over to Gilbert. Annual 
water allocations per acre are determined by SRP based upon reservoir storage conditions and are generally sufficient 
to meet On-Project water demands. 
 
In 1990, Gilbert entered into a Water Delivery and Use Agreement (“WDUA”) with SRP, which governs the Town’s 
access to water supplies controlle d or stored by SRP.  The WDUA  is considered a long-term supply of water under 
the Arizona Department of Water Resources (“ADWR”) Assured Water Supply (“AWS”) requirements.

Roosevelt Water Conservation District:  The Roosevelt Water Conservation District (“RWCD”) service area extends 
throughout portions of Gilbert as well as the Cities of Mesa, A rizona and Chandler, Arizona. RWCD lands within 
Gilbert's planning boundary extend from the Eastern Canal to th e RWCD Canal. Operationally, RWCD is similar to 
SRP in that RWCD water must be used on RWCD lands only. Pursuant to an agreement between SRP and RWCD in 
1924, and amended in 2010 to extend the agreement to 2134, RWCD  agreed to line portions of SRP’s canal system. 
In return, RWCD receives an entitlement to Salt and Verde River  water equivalent to 5.6 percent of SRP water 
diversions at the Granite Reef Dam. This entitlement is then distributed through a system of shared SRP and RWCD 
canals to the lands within RWCD. 
 
In a manner similar to the SRP WDUA, Gilbert obtains access to RWCD water under provisions of a Domestic Water 
Services Agreement with RWCD. In general, as lands within the R WCD are urbanized, currently totaling more than 
16,000 acres, the surface water component that was used by irrigators is made available to Gilbert for municipal use. 
RWCD water can only be used on RWCD lands. The amount of RWCD water to which Gilbert is entitled varies from 
year to year based on the 5.6 percent rule. For AWS purposes, this volume is set at 7,794 acre-feet per year. 
 
Colorado River Supplies:  The CAP is designed to deliver approximately 1.5 million acre-feet (“MAF”) of Colorado 
River water to central and southern Arizona. The estimated annual water supply available for delivery from the CAP 
in normal water years is 1.415 MAF. A total of 555,801 AF has b een contracted by municipal and infrastructure  
(“M&I”) entities, 462,801 AF are committed to Native American Communities, and 22,521 AF are under contract for 
agricultural purposes. 
 
Gilbert has a subcontract with the Central Arizona Water Conser vation District (“CAWCD”) for 7,235 AF of M&I 
priority CAP water. As a part of the Salt River Pima-Maricopa I ndian Community water rights settlement, Gilbert 
received 4,088 AF of Native Amer ican Community Priority CAP lea se water, and 6,424 AF of Wellton-Mohawk 
Exchange Water. The Wellton-Mohawk Water Right pre-dates the 1968 CAP authorization, and therefore is a senior 
Water Right. Also through the settlement, RWCD agreed to deliver a portion of their CAP water to several cities in 
the Phoenix area. Gilbert received 1,537 AF. Gilbert has a 100-year Native American Community lease with the San 
Carlos Apache Tribe for 5,925 AF that was executed in 2019. In 2021, Gilbert added 1,832 AF of Non-Indian 
Agricultural priority water from the State. CAP surface water is considered a long-term reliable supply. 
 
Gilbert has an additional Native American Community lease pendi ng for its water resources portfolio, the White 
Mountain Apache Tribe (“WMAT”) lease.  In 2008, Gilbert entered into an agreement with the WMAT for lease water 
obtained through an exchange of SRP and RWCD surface water. The  WMAT supply is a 100-year lease amounting 
to 4,226 AF and is estimated to be available in 2025.   
 
Gilbert’s current CAP supplies total 27,041 AF, and within thre e years are planned to grow to 31,267 AF. These 
supplies are delivered to the Town’s Water Treatment Plants for  delivery to customers. Gilb ert can also store these 
supplies underground at recharge facilities nearby to be pumped out later using Gilbert’s wells. 
 
Groundwater:  The AWS rules adopted by ADWR require that for a groundwater resource to be considered physically 
available, it must not cause the water table to drop below 1,00 0 feet below land surface over a 100-year pumping 
period. On September 29, 2010, Gilbert received its re-designation of AWS effective through year-end 2025.  Gilbert's 
legal availability of groundwater is limited by Arizona's 1980 Groundwater Management Act, which includes the 
volume of groundwater in the Town's AWS Groundwater Allowance Account. The account includes groundwater in 
the following categories: 
 
1. Gr
oundwater allowance account (1,785 AF per year) 
2. Accrued incidental recharge (3,200 AF per year) 
3. Long-Term Storage Credits (“LTSC”) (537,000 AF)  
 
Gilbert has been recharging reclaimed water and excess CAP supp lies to develop a recharge credit “bank account.” 
The Town stores water in CAP facilities, the Riparian Preserve,  the Neely Recharge Facility, and the South Area 
Recharge Facility. Gilbert also partners with multiple irrigation districts in the East Valley in the “In Lieu” recharge 
program. In this program, Gilbert orders its unused CAP water t o be delivered to an irrigation district, who then 
delivers that water to their farm ers, which reduces the district’s need to pump groundwater and in turn reduces their 
cost to deliver water to their customers. Each irrigation district that participates with Gilbert pays the Town a per AF 
assessment on each AF delivered, plus Gilbert earns LTSC for the amount of groundwater not pumped. If the credits A-4 
are not used in the year they are stored, they become LTSCs. Th ese credits can be used to offset future groundwater 
pumping. 
 
Annual credits and LTSCs are accr ued by recharging renewable su pplies (CAP and reclaimed water), which can be 
used to offset groundwater pumping. Groundwater pumped that cannot be offset by annual credits or LTSC incurs a 
replenishment obligation through Gilbert’s membership in the Central Arizona Groundwater Replenishment District 
(“CAGRD”). CAGRD is a department within the CAWCD that acts as a replenishment contractor for water providers 
located in CAP's tri-county area of Maricopa, Pinal and Pima Counties. Water providers who are unable to meet their 
service area demands without pumping groundwater in excess of t heir allowable limits can join CAGRD, who will 
then replenish the amount of groundwater pumped over the water provider's yearly limit at a current rate of $768/AF. 
Gilbert maintains membership in CAGRD to be used only if the Town is unable to acquire additional long-term 
renewable supplies and begins relying on LTSC’s to offset groundwater pumping over the statutory limit.  
 
Reclaimed Water:  Since 1985, the Town has been treating wastewater to produce a reclaimed water supply that is 
either delivered directly to cust omers or recharged to provide storage credits to offset g roundwater withdrawals. 
Gilbert uses 100 percent of the reclaimed water produced. The goal of Gilbert's reclaimed water management program 
is to beneficially use all of the reclaimed water produced by the Town through either reuse or recharge. Reclaimed 
water usage is designated for non-potable water uses such as landscape irrigation and other aesthetic uses. Irrigation 
water demands generate a seasonal water demand curve, with peak  demands occurring during the summer months, 
and low demands during the winter or during precipitation events. Since the reclaimed water produced from the Water 
Reclamation Plant’s is relatively constant, storage and recovery facilities need to be provided to manage the reclaimed 
water supply versus the seasonal demands. Gilbert currently has several recharge facilities available in which to store 
excess reclaimed water for later recovery to meet demands or to  be banked in Gilbert's LTSC account to be used to 
offset excess groundwater withdrawals. Approximately half of Gilbert’s reclaimed water is used directly for irrigation 
and half is recharged to offset groundwater pumping. Totaling approximately 15,000 AF currently, this supply grows 
along with the community, as it is reclaimed wastewater from our customers.  Gilbert’s 2021 long-term water supply 
totaled just over 78,000 AF, and its demand was 61,500 AF. 
 
Drought Preparation 
 
Gilbert maintains a Town Council approved Water Supply Reduction Management Plan which is updated periodically. 
The plan identifies water demand reduction responses that Gilbe rt will implement in the case of long-term surface 
water supply interruptions. The goal of the plan is to ensure adequate water service that meets customers’ needs with 
the available supplies and infrastructure. Gilbert will utilize its full well capacity and remaining surface water supplies, 
but if the water supplies are not enough, customers will be asked to reduce use in stages, depending on the severity of 
water supply reductions. Because the plan sets forth triggers for each stage and the accompanying demand reduction 
measures, customers w ill not face uncertainty regarding which m easures Gilbert will undertake to ensure reliable 
service. A copy of the Town’s Water Supply Reduction Management  Plan can be found at: 
https://www.gilbertaz.gov/home/showpublisheddocument/41870/637643885794770000. 
 
Water Quality 
 
The Town’s water quality departm ent operates a S tate-certified compliance laboratory used to ensure the Town’s 
water supply meets rigorous state and federal water quality regulations.  Samples are collected from the water 
treatment plants, well sites and dedicated water quality sample  stations throughout the Town and tested to ensure 
quality, safety and compliance.  Any other specialized testing is done through a certified drinking water testing 
laboratory off-site for more in-depth analysis.  In addition, the Town monitors water quality through additional testing 
for bacteriological and inorganic contaminants and organic materials.  This is used to optimize surface water treatment 
plant operations to adjust to any changes in incoming water qua lity and guarantee safe drinking water.  The Town 
continuously monitors water quality parameters at the two treatment plants as well as across the 19 well sites and 15 
water storage reservoirs.  The Town’s annual water quality repo rts can be found at: 
http://www.gilbertaz.gov/departments/public-works/water/water-qualityreports.

THE WASTEWATER SYSTEM 
The Wastewater System has 49 full time employees and serves app roximately 55 square miles within the Town’s 
existing corporate limits.  At the end of fiscal year 2020/21, there were 82,608 wastewater accounts, 79,549 of which 
were single-family residential, 693 were multi-family residential, 2,126 were commercial/industrial, 161 were schools 
and 79 were municipal. 
The Town is responsible for maintenance and operation of the co llection portion of the Wastewater System (mains 
and lift stations), and the reclaimed reuse portion of the Wast ewater System.  The effluent reuse portion of the 
Wastewater System includes both percolation and recharge wells,  as well as a  reuse distribution system to major 
irrigation users. 
The Greenfield Water Reclamation Plant 
The Greenfield Water Reclamation Plant (“GWRP”) is located in S outheast Gilbert and is a joint partnership with 
Mesa and Queen Creek and is operated by Mesa.  The plant currently can treat   30 MGD with an eventual projected 
capacity of 55.6 MGD.  Recent plant improvements increased Gilbert’s ownership in the GWRP from 8 MGD to 12 
MGD.  See “SYSTEM IMPROVEMENTS” for a description of GWRP impro vements.  At full build-out it is 
anticipated that the Town will own 16.4 MGD, Mesa will own 27 MGD and Queen Creek will own 12.2 MGD of the 
total capacity. 
GWRP produces class A+ reclaimed water per standards set by the  Arizona State Department of Environmental 
Quality.  The Town’s portion of the reclaimed water is sent to a nearby recharge facility and  direct reuse customers 
for irrigation use.    
The Neely Wastewater Reclamation Facility 
The Neely Wastewater Reclamation Facility (“NWRF” or “Neely”) processes wastewater for the Northwest areas of 
the Town.  The NWRF’s present capacity is 11 MGD.  While the To wn’s potable water supply and distribution 
facilities and the wastewater collection and effluent reuse fac ilities have been operated by Town staff, Neely is 
operated by Inframark, LLC (“Inframark”).  The Town negotiated an Agreement for Operations and Maintenance 
Services (the “Operating Agreement”) with Inframark for the ope ration of NWRF.  Inframark is an established 
operator of public water and wastewater treatment facilities and systems and is currently operating similar facilities in 
the United States. 
Under the terms of the Operating Agreement, the arrangement wit h Inframark will be renewed each year unless the 
Town gives 60 days written notice to Inframark of its intention  to terminate the Operating Agreement.  Under the 
terms of the Operating Agreement, Inframark is responsible for routine maintenance and the Town is responsible for 
“extraordinary costs” defined as any single item exceeding $5,000 and subject to a cap on costs based on the Consumer 
Price Index.  In addition, in the Operating Agreement, Inframar k agrees to indemnify the Town for wrongful death, A-8 
personal injury, property damage or economic loss arising from the negligent acts or omissions of Inframark in 
connection with the performance of its obligations under the Operating Agreement. 
Recharge Facilities 
The Town has pioneered the process of percolation recharge and injection recharge of treated effluent into the ground 
water table as a form of banking LTSC.  This is in addition to the effluent reuse water system which is used to irrigate 
large parks, open spaces and golf courses in the Town.  The Tow n operates groundwater recharge facilities with a 
current combined capacity of 20.6 MGD.  The Town’s recharge fac ilities consist of percolation basins and injection 
wells that deliver reclaimed water to the aquifer through infiltration.  Current recharge facilities and their capacities 
are as follows: 
1. Neely  – 1.6 MGD  
2. Riparian Preserve – 8 MGD 
3. South Recharge Site – 9 MGD 
4. Vadose zone injection wells (2) – 2 MGD 
 
The Town also participates in water recharge at other facilitie s throughout the Phoenix metropolitan area including: 
3% of the Granite Reef Underground Storage Project at 3,000 AF of recharge capacity per year; and the Superstition,  
Agua Fria and Tonopah Recharge projects owned by the CAWCD.

SYSTEM DEVELOPMENT FEES 
 
In an effort to ensure that the growth driven capital and infrastructure needs are funded by growth, the Town adopted 
comprehensive SDFs in 1997. The fees for water, wastewater, par ks and recreation, general government, 
transportation and public safety are collected at the time a bu ilding permit is issued for residential, commercial and 
other non-residential development.  
 
Most SDFs are calculated on a uniform basis for all new develop ment. Growth-related projects are considered as 
increases in current system capacity rather than as specific improvements for any particular geographic location within 
the Town.  The only exception is for wastewater which is broken  out into the two service areas: Neely and GWRP. 
These service areas have unique costs of service and the SDFs are calculated independently for the two service areas 
to account for this. 
 
Authorization and Purpose 
 
Arizona Revised Statutes Section 9-463.05 authorizes SDFs to fund capital improvements only and SDFs may not be 
used to fund operating expenses. The amount of the SDF must bea r a reasonable relationship to the burden imposed 
upon the municipality to provide additional necessary public services to the development.  
 
SDFs are calculated based on the annual Capital Improvement Pla n and Infrastructure Improvement Plan. In some 
cases, depending on the timing and financial requirements of ea ch project, borrowing may also be required. In those 
cases, all of the borrowing and project costs are included in t he amount to be funded through SDFs. In other words, 
projects that cannot be funded through the revenues generated b y new construction permit activity, on a pay as you 
go basis, are also funded through borrowing. Projects in this c ategory have traditionally been larger capital projects, 
such as expansions of the Water and Wastewater Treatment Plants. 
 
System Development Fee Schedule 
 
The Town’s water, water resources and wastewater SDFs were adopted March 2022 and take effect June 2022.  The 
Town is currently working with an outside consulting firm to do  a comprehensive update of its infrastructure 
improvement plan and all SDFs.

APPENDIX B 
 
TOWN OF GILBERT, ARIZONA 
GENERAL ECONOMIC AND DEMOGRAPHIC INFORMATION 
 
 
The Town is located in the southeastern portion of Maricopa County, Arizona (the “County”), bounded on the north and east 
by Mesa, Arizona, on the west by Chandler, Arizona, on the southeast by Queen Creek, Arizona and on the south by the Gila 
River Indian Community. Founded in 1902 and incorporated on Jul y 6, 1920, the Town today h as a planning area of 72.6 
square miles. The population of the Town nearly doubled in the 2000s.  The following table illustrates respective population 
statistics for the Town, the County and the State: 
 
POPULATION STATISTICS
